Capital city of Taiwan  
This article is about the city in Taiwan. For other uses, see [Taipei (disambiguation)](/wiki/Taipei_(disambiguation) "Taipei (disambiguation)").  
Not to be confused with [New Taipei City](/wiki/New_Taipei_City "New Taipei City").

<br />

**Taipei** ([/ˌtaɪˈpeɪ/](/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English") [](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/ee/LL-Q1860_%28eng%29-Vealhurl-Taipei.wav/LL-Q1860_%28eng%29-Vealhurl-Taipei.wav.mp3 "Play audio")^[ⓘ](/wiki/File:LL-Q1860_(eng)-Vealhurl-Taipei.wav "File:LL-Q1860 (eng)-Vealhurl-Taipei.wav")^; [Chinese](/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 臺北; [pinyin](/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): *Táiběi* ),^[\[4\]](#cite_note-5)^ officially **Taipei City** ,^[\[I\]](#cite_note-word1-1)^ is the [capital](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city")^[\[a\]](#cite_note-9)^ and a [special municipality](/wiki/Special_municipality_(Taiwan) "Special municipality (Taiwan)") of [Taiwan](/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan").^[\[7\]](#cite_note-gov-8)^^[\[8\]](#cite_note-10)^ Located in [Northern Taiwan](/wiki/Regions_of_Taiwan "Regions of Taiwan"), Taipei City is an [enclave](/wiki/Enclave "Enclave") of the municipality of [New Taipei City](/wiki/New_Taipei_City "New Taipei City") that sits about 25 km (16 mi) southwest of the northern port city of [Keelung](/wiki/Keelung "Keelung"). Most of the city rests on the [Taipei Basin](/wiki/Taipei_Basin "Taipei Basin"), an ancient lakebed. The basin is bounded by the relatively narrow valleys of the [Keelung](/wiki/Keelung_River "Keelung River") and [Xindian rivers](/wiki/Xindian_River "Xindian River"), which join to form the [Tamsui River](/wiki/Tamsui_River "Tamsui River") along the city's western border.^[\[9\]](#cite_note-tcggeo-11)^{#cite_ref-tcggeo_11-0}

The municipality of Taipei is home to an estimated population of 2,494,813 (March 2023),^[\[10\]](#cite_note-population-12)^ forming the core part of the [Taipei--Keelung metropolitan area](/wiki/Taipei%E2%80%93Keelung_metropolitan_area "Taipei–Keelung metropolitan area"), also known as "Greater Taipei", which includes the nearby cities of New Taipei and Keelung with a population of 7,047,559,^[\[10\]](#cite_note-population-12)^^[\[11\]](#cite_note-13)^ the 40th most-populous urban area in the world---roughly one-third of Taiwanese citizens live in the metro areas. The name "Taipei" can refer either to the whole metropolitan area or just the municipality alone. Taipei has been the political center of the island since 1887, when it first became the seat of [Taiwan Province](/wiki/Taiwan_Province "Taiwan Province") by [the Qing dynasty](/wiki/Taiwan_under_Qing_rule "Taiwan under Qing rule") until 1895 and again from 1945 to 1956 by the [Republic of China (ROC) government](/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_China "Government of the Republic of China"),^[\[b\]](#cite_note-14)^ with an [interregnum](/wiki/Interregnum "Interregnum") from 1895 to 1945 as the seat of the [Government-General of Taiwan](/wiki/Government-General_of_Taiwan "Government-General of Taiwan") during [the Japanese rule](/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule "Taiwan under Japanese rule"). The city has been the national seat of the [ROC central government](/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_China "Government of the Republic of China") since 1949, and it became the nation's first special municipality (then known as Yuan-controlled municipality) on 1 July 1967, upgrading from [provincial city](/wiki/Provincial_city_(Taiwan) "Provincial city (Taiwan)") status.{#cite_ref-14}

Taipei is the [economic](/wiki/Economy_of_Taiwan "Economy of Taiwan"), [political](/wiki/Politics_of_the_Republic_of_China "Politics of the Republic of China"), [educational](/wiki/Education_in_Taiwan "Education in Taiwan") and [cultural](/wiki/Culture_of_Taiwan "Culture of Taiwan") center of Taiwan. It has been rated an "Alpha − City" by [GaWC](/wiki/GaWC "GaWC").^[\[12\]](#cite_note-15)^ Taipei also forms a major part of a high-tech industrial area.^[\[13\]](#cite_note-16)^ [Railways](/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Taiwan "Rail transport in Taiwan"), [highways](/wiki/Highway_system_in_Taiwan "Highway system in Taiwan"), airports and bus lines connect Taipei with all parts of the island. The city is served by two airports -- [Songshan](/wiki/Songshan_Airport "Songshan Airport") and [Taoyuan](/wiki/Taoyuan_International_Airport "Taoyuan International Airport"). The municipality is home to architectural and cultural landmarks, including [Taipei 101](/wiki/Taipei_101 "Taipei 101") (which was formerly the tallest building in the world), [Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall](/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek_Memorial_Hall "Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall"), [Dalongdong Baoan Temple](/wiki/Dalongdong_Baoan_Temple "Dalongdong Baoan Temple"), [Hsing Tian Kong](/wiki/Hsing_Tian_Kong "Hsing Tian Kong"), [Lungshan Temple of Manka](/wiki/Lungshan_Temple_of_Manka "Lungshan Temple of Manka"), [National Palace Museum](/wiki/National_Palace_Museum "National Palace Museum"), [Presidential Office Building](/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building_(Republic_of_China) "Presidential Office Building (Republic of China)"), [Taipei Guest House](/wiki/Taipei_Guest_House "Taipei Guest House") and [Zhinan Temple](/wiki/Zhinan_Temple "Zhinan Temple"). [Shopping districts](/wiki/Shopping_districts "Shopping districts") including [Ximending](/wiki/Ximending "Ximending") as well as several [night markets](/wiki/Night_markets_in_Taiwan "Night markets in Taiwan") dispersed throughout the city. Natural features include [Maokong](/wiki/Maokong "Maokong"), [Yangmingshan](/wiki/Yangmingshan "Yangmingshan") and [hot springs](/wiki/Taiwanese_hot_springs "Taiwanese hot springs").{#cite_ref-16}

In English-language news reports, the name *Taipei* often serves as a [synecdoche](/wiki/Synecdoche "Synecdoche") referring to the central government that controls the [Taiwan Area](/wiki/Taiwan_Area "Taiwan Area"). Due to the ambiguous [political status of Taiwan](/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan "Political status of Taiwan") internationally, the term *[Chinese Taipei](/wiki/Chinese_Taipei "Chinese Taipei")* is also frequently used as a [synonym](/wiki/Synonym "Synonym") for the entire country, as when Taiwan's governmental representatives participate in [international organizations](/wiki/International_organizations "International organizations") or when Taiwan's athletes compete in international sporting events, including the [Olympics](/wiki/Olympic_Games "Olympic Games").  

Names {#Names}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Names")\]  
See also: [Chinese language romanization in Taiwan](/wiki/Chinese_language_romanization_in_Taiwan "Chinese language romanization in Taiwan")

The spellings *Taipei* and *Tʻai-pei* derive from the [Wade--Giles](/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles "Wade–Giles") romanization *Tʻai²-pei³* ^[\[14\]](#cite_note-17)^ which means *the North of Taiwan* in Chinese. The name could be also romanized as *Táiběi* according to [Hanyu Pinyin](/wiki/Hanyu_Pinyin "Hanyu Pinyin") and [Tongyong Pinyin](/wiki/Tongyong_Pinyin "Tongyong Pinyin").^[\[15\]](#cite_note-18)^^[\[16\]](#cite_note-19)^^[\[17\]](#cite_note-20)^{#cite_ref-20}

The city has also been known as *Tai-pak* ^[\[18\]](#cite_note-21)^^[\[19\]](#cite_note-22)^ (derived from [Taiwanese Hokkien](/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien "Taiwanese Hokkien")) and *Taipeh* .^[\[20\]](#cite_note-23)^^[\[21\]](#cite_note-24)^{#cite_ref-24}

During the [Japanese rule](/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule "Taiwan under Japanese rule") from 1895 to 1945, Taipei was known as *Taihoku* , which is the pronunciation of the [Chinese characters](/wiki/Chinese_characters "Chinese characters") ([Kanji](/wiki/Kanji "Kanji"): [台北](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97 "wikt:台北")) for Taipei in Japanese.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-25)^{#cite_ref-25}  

History {#History}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: History")\]  
Main article: [History of Taipei](/wiki/History_of_Taipei "History of Taipei")  
See also: [North-South divide in Taiwan § Taipei](/wiki/North-South_divide_in_Taiwan#Taipei "North-South divide in Taiwan")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/North_Side_of_Old_Taipei_City_North_Gate.jpg/215px-North_Side_of_Old_Taipei_City_North_Gate.jpg)](/wiki/File:North_Side_of_Old_Taipei_City_North_Gate.jpg) Taipei's Old North Gate, completed in 1884

Prior to the significant influx of Han Chinese colonists, the region of [Taipei Basin](/wiki/Taipei_Basin "Taipei Basin") was mainly inhabited by the [plains aborigines](/wiki/Taiwanese_plains_aborigines "Taiwanese plains aborigines") called [Ketagalan](/wiki/Ketagalan "Ketagalan"). The number of Han colonists gradually increased in the early 18th century under [Qing dynasty rule](/wiki/Taiwan_under_Qing_rule "Taiwan under Qing rule") after the government began permitting development in the area.^[\[23\]](#cite_note-26)^ In 1875, the northern part of the island was incorporated into the new [Taipeh Prefecture](/wiki/Taipeh_Prefecture "Taipeh Prefecture").{#cite_ref-26}

It was formerly established as Taipeh-fu and was the temporary capital of the island in 1887 when it was declared a province ([Fukien-Taiwan Province](/wiki/Taiwan_Province#Qing_Dynasty "Taiwan Province")).^[\[24\]](#cite_note-27)^^[\[25\]](#cite_note-28)^ Taipeh was formally made the provincial capital in 1894. The romanized transcription of Taipeh was changed to Taihoku in 1895 when the Empire of Japan annexed Taiwan, based on the Japanese reading of the two characters. The writing in Chinese characters remained unaltered. Under Japanese rule, the city was administered under [Taihoku Prefecture](/wiki/Taihoku_Prefecture "Taihoku Prefecture"). Taiwan's Japanese rulers embarked on an extensive program of advanced [urban planning](/wiki/Urban_planning "Urban planning") that featured extensive railroad links. A number of Taipei landmarks and cultural institutions date from this period.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-marsh1-29)^{#cite_ref-marsh1_29-0}

Following the [surrender of Japan](/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan "Surrender of Japan") to the [Allies](/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") during 1945, effective control of Taiwan was [handed to the Republic of China (ROC)](/wiki/History_of_Taiwan_since_1945 "History of Taiwan since 1945"). After facing defeat from Communist forces, the ruling [Kuomintang](/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang") relocated the [ROC government](/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_China "Government of the Republic of China") to Taiwan and declared Taipei the [provisional capital](/wiki/Provisional_capital "Provisional capital") of the ROC in December 1949.^[\[27\]](#cite_note-ng-30)^^[\[28\]](#cite_note-bbctimeline-retreat-31)^^[\[29\]](#cite_note-32)^ Taiwan's Kuomintang rulers regarded the city as the capital of [Taiwan Province](/wiki/Taiwan_Province "Taiwan Province") and their control as mandated by [General Order No. 1](/wiki/General_Order_No._1 "General Order No. 1").{#cite_ref-32}

In 1990, Taipei provided the backdrop for the [Wild Lily student rallies](/wiki/Wild_Lily_student_movement "Wild Lily student movement") that moved Taiwanese society from one-party rule to multi-party [democracy](/wiki/Democracy "Democracy") by [1996](/wiki/1996_Taiwan_presidential_election "1996 Taiwan presidential election"). The city has served as the seat of Taiwan's democratically elected national government ever since.  

### Early settlers--Qing dynasty {#Early_settlers.E2.80.93Qing_dynasty}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Early settlers–Qing dynasty")\]

Prior to the 18th century, the region known as the [Taipei Basin](/wiki/Taipei_Basin "Taipei Basin") was home to [Ketagalan](/wiki/Ketagalan_people "Ketagalan people") tribes.^[\[30\]](#cite_note-33)^ [Han Chinese](/wiki/Han_Chinese "Han Chinese") colonists from [Dabu County](/wiki/Dabu_County "Dabu County"), [Yongding County](/wiki/Yongding_County "Yongding County"), [Anxi](/wiki/Anxi_County "Anxi County") and [Tong'an](/wiki/Tong%27an "Tong'an") of [Southern Fujian](/wiki/Southern_Fujian "Southern Fujian") began to settle in the Taipei Basin in 1709.^[\[31\]](#cite_note-kelly-34)^^[\[32\]](#cite_note-tcghistory-35)^{#cite_ref-tcghistory_35-0}

In the late 19th century, the Taipei area, where the major Han Chinese settlements in northern Taiwan and one of the designated overseas trade ports, [Tamsui](/wiki/Tamsui_District "Tamsui District"), were located, gained economic importance due to the booming overseas trade, especially that of [tea](/wiki/Tea "Tea") export. In 1875, the northern part of Taiwan was separated from [Taiwan Prefecture](/wiki/Taiwan_Prefecture "Taiwan Prefecture") and incorporated into the new [Taipeh Prefecture](/wiki/Taipeh_Prefecture "Taipeh Prefecture") as a new administrative entity of the Qing dynasty.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-marsh1-29)^ Having been established adjoining the flourishing townships of [Bangka](/wiki/Wanhua_District "Wanhua District"), [Dalongdong](/wiki/Dalongdong "Dalongdong"), and [Twatutia](/wiki/Twatutia "Twatutia"), the new prefectural capital was known as *Chengnei* ([Chinese](/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 城內; [pinyin](/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): *chéngnèi* ; [Pe̍h-ōe-jī](/wiki/Pe%CC%8Dh-%C5%8De-j%C4%AB "Pe̍h-ōe-jī"): *siâⁿ-lāi* ), "the inner city", and government buildings were erected there. From 1875 until the beginning of Japanese rule in 1895, Taipei was part of Tamsui County of Taipeh Prefecture and the prefectural capital.^[\[33\]](#cite_note-36)^{#cite_ref-36}

In 1885, as work commenced to govern the island as a province, Taipeh was thus temporarily designated as a provincial capital. The city officially became the capital in 1894.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ Nowadays, all that remains from the historical period is the north gate. The west gate and [city walls](/wiki/Taipei_City_Walls "Taipei City Walls") were demolished by the Japanese while the south gate, little south gate, and east gate were extensively modified by the [Kuomintang](/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang") and have lost much of their original character.^[\[34\]](#cite_note-37)^{#cite_ref-37}  

### Empire of Japan {#Empire_of_Japan}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Empire of Japan")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Txu-pclmaps-oclc-6550514-taihoku-east-2422-iii.jpg/220px-Txu-pclmaps-oclc-6550514-taihoku-east-2422-iii.jpg)](/wiki/File:Txu-pclmaps-oclc-6550514-taihoku-east-2422-iii.jpg) Map of eastern Taipei (labeled as TAIHOKU) and nearby areas ([AMS](/wiki/Army_Map_Service "Army Map Service"), 1944) [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg/220px-%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg)](/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg) The [Taihoku Prefecture](/wiki/Taihoku_Prefecture "Taihoku Prefecture") government building in the 1910s (now the [Control Yuan](/wiki/Control_Yuan "Control Yuan") building)

As settlement for losing the [First Sino-Japanese War](/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War "First Sino-Japanese War"), China ceded the [island of Taiwan](/wiki/Island_of_Taiwan "Island of Taiwan") to the [Empire of Japan](/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan") in 1895 as part of the [Treaty of Shimonoseki](/wiki/Treaty_of_Shimonoseki "Treaty of Shimonoseki"). After the Japanese takeover, Taipei, romanized into English as **Taihoku** following the Japanese language pronunciation, was retained as the capital. It subsequently emerged as the political center of the Japanese Colonial Government.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-marsh1-29)^ During that time the city acquired the characteristics of an administrative center, including many new public buildings and [housing for civil servants](/wiki/Qidong_Street_Japanese_Houses "Qidong Street Japanese Houses"). Much of the architecture of Taipei dates from the period of [Japanese rule](/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule "Taiwan under Japanese rule"), including the [Presidential Office Building](/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building_(Republic_of_China) "Presidential Office Building (Republic of China)") which was the Office of the [Governor-General of Taiwan](/wiki/Governor-General_of_Taiwan "Governor-General of Taiwan").{#cite_ref-marsh1_29-2}

During Japanese rule, Taihoku was incorporated in 1920 as part of [Taihoku Prefecture](/wiki/Taihoku_Prefecture "Taihoku Prefecture"). It included [Bangka](/wiki/Wanhua_District "Wanhua District"), [Twatutia](/wiki/Twatutia "Twatutia"), and *Jōnai* (城內) among other small settlements. The eastern village of *Matsuyama* (松山庄, modern-day [Songshan District, Taipei](/wiki/Songshan_District,_Taipei "Songshan District, Taipei")) was annexed into Taihoku City in 1938. Taihoku and surrounding areas were bombed by Allied forces on several occasions. The largest of these Allied air raids, the [Taihoku Air Raid](/wiki/Taihoku_Air_Raid "Taihoku Air Raid"), took place on 31 May 1945.  

### Post-WW2 under ROC {#Post-WW2_under_ROC}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: Post-WW2 under ROC")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Taipei_2012_3_amk.jpg/170px-Taipei_2012_3_amk.jpg)](/wiki/File:Taipei_2012_3_amk.jpg) [Taipei 101](/wiki/Taipei_101 "Taipei 101") is a landmark and tourist attraction in Taipei. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg/200px-Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg)](/wiki/File:Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg) The [National Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall](/wiki/National_Chiang_Kai-shek_Memorial_Hall "National Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall") is a national monument, landmark, and tourist attraction in Taipei. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg/220px-U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg)](/wiki/File:U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg) With President [Chiang Kai-shek](/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek"), U.S. President [Dwight D. Eisenhower](/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower "Dwight D. Eisenhower") waved to a crowd during his visit to Taipei in June 1960.

Upon the Japanese defeat following the nuclear bomb destruction of [Hiroshima](/wiki/Hiroshima "Hiroshima") and its consequent surrender in August 1945, the [Kuomintang](/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang") (Chinese Nationalist Party) [assumed control](/wiki/Retrocession_of_Taiwan "Retrocession of Taiwan") of Taiwan. Subsequently, Taipei was established as a [provincial city](/wiki/Provincial_city_(Taiwan) "Provincial city (Taiwan)") and a temporary Office of the [Taiwan Province](/wiki/Taiwan_Province "Taiwan Province") Administrative Governor was established in it.^[\[35\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh199685-38)^ In 1947 the [Kuomintang](/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang") (KMT) government under [Chiang Kai-shek](/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek") declared island-wide [martial law in Taiwan](/wiki/Martial_law_in_Taiwan "Martial law in Taiwan") as a result of the [28 February Incident](/wiki/28_February_Incident "28 February Incident"), which began with incidents in Taipei but led to an island-wide crackdown on the local population by forces loyal to Chiang. Two years later, on 7 December 1949, Chiang and the Kuomintang forces were forced to flee mainland China after the defeat by Communist revolutionaries. The KMT-led national government that fled to Taiwan declared Taipei to be the provisional capital of a continuing Republic of China.^[\[27\]](#cite_note-ng-30)^^[\[28\]](#cite_note-bbctimeline-retreat-31)^{#cite_ref-bbctimeline-retreat_31-1}

Taipei [expanded greatly](/wiki/Military_dependents%27_village "Military dependents' village") in the decades after 1949, and as approved on 30 December 1966, by the [Executive Yuan](/wiki/Executive_Yuan "Executive Yuan"), Taipei was declared a [special municipality](/wiki/Special_municipality_(Taiwan) "Special municipality (Taiwan)") on 1 July 1967.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-tcghistory-35)^ In the following year, Taipei City expanded again by annexing [Shilin](/wiki/Shilin_District "Shilin District"), [Beitou](/wiki/Beitou_District "Beitou District"), [Neihu](/wiki/Neihu_District "Neihu District"), [Nangang](/wiki/Nangang_District,_Taipei "Nangang District, Taipei"), [Jingmei](/wiki/Jingmei "Jingmei"), and [Muzha](/wiki/Muzha_District "Muzha District"). At that time, the city's total area increased fourfold by absorbing several outlying towns and villages and the population increased to 1.56 million people.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-tcghistory-35)^{#cite_ref-tcghistory_35-2}

The city's population, which had reached one million in the early 1960s, also expanded rapidly after 1967, exceeding two million by the mid-1970s. Although growth within the city itself gradually slowed thereafter^[\[35\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh199685-38)^ --- its population had become relatively stable by the mid-1990s -- Taipei remained one of the world's most densely populated urban areas, and the population continued to increase in the region surrounding the city, notably along the corridor between Taipei and [Keelung](/wiki/Keelung "Keelung").^\[*[original research?](/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research "Wikipedia:No original research")*\]^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh199685_38-1}

In 1990, Taipei's 16 districts were consolidated into the current 12 districts.^[\[36\]](#cite_note-yearbook-39)^ [Mass democracy rallies](/wiki/Wild_Lily_student_movement "Wild Lily student movement") that year in the [plaza](/wiki/Liberty_Square_(Taipei) "Liberty Square (Taipei)") around Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall led to an island-wide transition to multi-party [democracy](/wiki/Democracy "Democracy"), where legislators are chosen via regularly scheduled popular elections, during the presidency of [Lee Teng-Hui](/wiki/Lee_Teng-Hui "Lee Teng-Hui").^\[*[original research?](/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research "Wikipedia:No original research")*\]^{#cite_ref-yearbook_39-0}  

Geography {#Geography}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Geography")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei%27s_west_from_the_perspective_of_Tamsui_River.jpg/220px-Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei%27s_west_from_the_perspective_of_Tamsui_River.jpg)](/wiki/File:Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei%27s_west_from_the_perspective_of_Tamsui_River.jpg) Aerial panorama of Taipei's west from the perspective of Tamsui River [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2014-02-23_%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97_Taipei_from_%E8%B2%93%E7%A9%BA_01.jpg/220px-2014-02-23_%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97_Taipei_from_%E8%B2%93%E7%A9%BA_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:2014-02-23_%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97_Taipei_from_%E8%B2%93%E7%A9%BA_01.jpg) The city of Taipei, as seen from [Maokong](/wiki/Maokong "Maokong") in 2014

Taipei City is located in the [Taipei Basin](/wiki/Taipei_Basin "Taipei Basin") in northern [Taiwan](/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan").^[\[37\]](#cite_note-taipeiprofile-40)^ It is bordered by the [Xindian River](/wiki/Xindian_River "Xindian River") on the south and the [Tamsui River](/wiki/Tamsui_River "Tamsui River") on the west. The generally low-lying terrain of the central areas on the western side of the municipality slopes upward to the south and east and especially to the north,^[\[9\]](#cite_note-tcggeo-11)^ where it reaches the 1,120 m (3,670 ft)-tall [Qixing Mountain](/wiki/Qixing_Mountain_(Taipei) "Qixing Mountain (Taipei)"), the highest (dormant) [volcano](/wiki/Volcano "Volcano") in Taiwan in [Yangmingshan National Park](/wiki/Yangmingshan_National_Park "Yangmingshan National Park"). The northern districts of [Shilin](/wiki/Shilin_District "Shilin District") and [Beitou](/wiki/Beitou_District "Beitou District") extend north of the [Keelung River](/wiki/Keelung_River "Keelung River") and are bordered by Yangmingshan National Park. The Taipei city limits cover an area of 271.7997 km^2^ (104.9425 sq mi),^[\[38\]](#cite_note-41)^ ranking sixteenth of twenty-five among [all counties and cities in Taiwan](/wiki/List_of_Taiwanese_counties_and_cities_by_area "List of Taiwanese counties and cities by area").{#cite_ref-41}

Two peaks, Qixing Mountain and Mt. Datun, rise to the northeast of the city.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-geopop-42)^ Qixing Mountain is located on the [Tatun Volcanic Group](/wiki/Tatun_Volcanic_Group "Tatun Volcanic Group"); its 1,120 m (3,670 ft)-high main peak renders it the tallest mountain at the rim of the Taipei Basin; 1,092 m (3,583 ft)-high Mt. Datun is a close runner up. These former volcanoes make up the western section of Yangmingshan National Park, extending from Mt. Datun northward to Mt. Caigongkeng (菜公坑山). Located on a broad saddle between two mountains, the area also contains the marshy Datun Pond.{#cite_ref-geopop_42-0}

To the southeast of the city lie the Songshan Hills and the Qingshui Ravine, which form a barrier of lush woods.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-geopop-42)^{#cite_ref-geopop_42-1}  

### Climate {#Climate}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Climate")\]

|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 Climate chart ([explanation](/wiki/Template:Climate_chart/How_to_read_a_climate_chart "Template:Climate chart/How to read a climate chart"))                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| |----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|----------|----------| | J        | F         | M         | A         | M         | J         | J         | A         | S         | O         | N        | D        | | 94 20 14 | 129 21 15 | 158 23 16 | 151 27 19 | 245 30 23 | 355 33 25 | 214 35 27 | 337 34 27 | 337 32 25 | 163 28 23 | 89 25 20 | 97 21 16 | | █ Average max. and min. temperatures in °C                                                                                      |||||||||||| | █ Precipitation totals in mm                                                                                                    ||||||||||||                                                                                                                                    |
| |                                                      Imperial conversion                                                      |||||||||||| |-----------|-----------|-----------|---------|-----------|----------|-----------|----------|----------|-----------|-----------|-----------| | J         | F         | M         | A       | M         | J        | J         | A        | S        | O         | N         | D         | | 3.7 67 58 | 5.1 69 58 | 6.2 73 61 | 6 80 67 | 9.7 86 73 | 14 91 78 | 8.4 95 80 | 13 94 80 | 13 89 77 | 6.4 82 73 | 3.5 77 68 | 3.8 70 61 | | █ Average max. and min. temperatures in °F                                                                                    |||||||||||| | █ Precipitation totals in inches                                                                                              |||||||||||| |

Taipei has a [humid subtropical climate](/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate "Humid subtropical climate") ([Köppen](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification"): *Cfa* ).^[\[40\]](#cite_note-43)^^[\[41\]](#cite_note-44)^^[\[42\]](#cite_note-45)^^[\[43\]](#cite_note-46)^ Summers are long-lasting, very hot and humid, and accompanied by occasional heavy rainstorms and typhoons; while winters are short, generally warm and generally very [foggy](/wiki/Fog "Fog") due to the northeasterly winds from the vast [Siberian High](/wiki/Siberian_High "Siberian High") being intensified by the pooling of this cooler air in the Taipei Basin. As in the rest of Northern Taiwan, daytime temperatures of Taipei can often peak above 26 °C (79 °F) during a warm winter day, while they can dip below that same level during afternoon showers and thunderstorms in the summer. Occasional cold fronts during the winter months can drop the daily temperature by 3 to 5 °C (5.4 to 9.0 °F), though temperatures rarely drop below 10 °C (50 °F).^[\[44\]](#cite_note-47)^ Extreme temperatures ranged from −0.2 °C (31.6 °F) on 13 February 1901 to 39.7 °C (103.5 °F) on 24 July 2020, while snow has never been recorded in the city besides on mountains located within the city limit such as [Yangmingshan](/wiki/Yangmingshan "Yangmingshan"). Due to Taiwan's location in the Pacific Ocean, it is affected by the [Pacific typhoon](/wiki/Pacific_typhoon "Pacific typhoon") season, which occurs between June and October.{#cite_ref-47}  
{#cite_ref-CWBrecordlow2_52-0}

### Air quality {#Air_quality}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Air quality")\]

In comparison to other [Asian](/wiki/Asia "Asia") cities, Taipei has "excellent" capabilities for managing [air quality](/wiki/Air_quality "Air quality") in the city.^[\[50\]](#cite_note-53)^ Its rainy climate, location near the coast, and strong environmental regulations have prevented air pollution from becoming a substantial health issue, at least compared to cities in southeast Asia and industrial China. However, smog is extremely common and there is poor visibility throughout the city after rainless days.{#cite_ref-53}

Motor vehicle engine exhaust, particularly from motor scooters, is a source of [air pollution](/wiki/Air_pollution "Air pollution") in Taipei. There are higher levels of fine [particulate](/wiki/Particulate "Particulate") matter and [polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons](/wiki/Polycyclic_aromatic_hydrocarbon "Polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbon") in the mornings because of less air movement; sunlight reduces some pollution.^[\[51\]](#cite_note-54)^{#cite_ref-54}

Demographics {#Demographics}
----------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Demographics")\]

[Historical population]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg/220px-Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg)](/wiki/File:Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg) Customers in the [Shilin Night Market](/wiki/Shilin_Night_Market "Shilin Night Market")

While Taipei City is home to 2,524,393 people (2022), the greater [metropolitan area](/wiki/Taipei%E2%80%93Keelung_metropolitan_area "Taipei–Keelung metropolitan area") has a population of 7,047,559 people.^[\[10\]](#cite_note-population-12)^ Even though the population of the city has been decreasing in recent years, the population of adjacent [New Taipei](/wiki/New_Taipei "New Taipei") has been increasing. The population loss, while rapid in its early years, was slowed by lower density development and campaigns designed to increase the birthrate in the city in the 2010s. As a result, the population rose 2010--2015.^[\[10\]](#cite_note-population-12)^^[\[57\]](#cite_note-demographics-60)^^[\[58\]](#cite_note-61)^{#cite_ref-61}

Due to Taipei's geography and location in the [Taipei Basin](/wiki/Taipei_Basin "Taipei Basin") as well as differing times of settlement and differing degrees of economic development of its districts, Taipei's population is not evenly distributed. The districts of [Daan](/wiki/Daan_District,_Taipei_City "Daan District, Taipei City"), [Songshan](/wiki/Songshan_District,_Taipei "Songshan District, Taipei"), and [Datong](/wiki/Datong_District,_Taipei "Datong District, Taipei") are the most densely populated. These districts, along with adjacent communities such as [Yonghe](/wiki/Yonghe_District "Yonghe District") and [Zhonghe](/wiki/Zhonghe_District "Zhonghe District"), contain some of the most densely populated neighborhoods in the world.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-demographics-60)^{#cite_ref-demographics_60-1}

In 2008, the [crude birth rate](/wiki/Birth_rate "Birth rate") stood at 7.88%, while the [mortality rate](/wiki/Mortality_rate "Mortality rate") stood at 5.94%. A decreasing and rapidly aging population is an important issue for the city.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-demographics-60)^ By the end of 2009, one in ten people in Taipei was over 65 years of age.^[\[59\]](#cite_note-62)^ Residents who had obtained a college education or higher accounted for 43.48% of the population, and the literacy rate stood at 99.18%.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-demographics-60)^{#cite_ref-demographics_60-3}

Like the rest of Taiwan, Taipei is composed of four major ethnic subgroups: [Hoklos](/wiki/Hoklo_people "Hoklo people"), [Waishengren](/wiki/Waishengren "Waishengren"), [Hakkas](/wiki/Hakka_people "Hakka people"), and [aborigines](/wiki/Taiwanese_aborigines "Taiwanese aborigines").^[\[57\]](#cite_note-demographics-60)^ Although Hoklos and [Waishengren](/wiki/Waishengren "Waishengren") form the majority of the population of the city, in recent decades many Hakkas have moved into the city. The aboriginal population in the city stands at 16,713 at the end of 2018 (\<1%), concentrated mostly in the suburban districts. Foreigners (mainly from [Indonesia](/wiki/Indonesia "Indonesia"), the [Philippines](/wiki/Philippines "Philippines"), and [Japan](/wiki/Japan "Japan")) numbered 71,858 at the end of 2022.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-demographics-60)^^[\[60\]](#cite_note-63)^{#cite_ref-63}

| Age distribution |  Male   | Female  |  Total  |
|------------------|---------|---------|---------|

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Economy")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei_City%27s_west.jpg/220px-Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei_City%27s_west.jpg)](/wiki/File:Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei_City%27s_west.jpg) Aerial panorama of Taipei City's west  
See also: [Economy of Taiwan](/wiki/Economy_of_Taiwan "Economy of Taiwan")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg/220px-Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg) Bellavita Shopping Center and [CPC](/wiki/CPC_Corporation,_Taiwan "CPC Corporation, Taiwan") Building at [Xinyi Special District](/wiki/Xinyi_Business_Area "Xinyi Business Area") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg/220px-Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg)](/wiki/File:Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg) Taipei [Neihu](/wiki/Neihu_District "Neihu District") Technology Park

As Taiwan's business, financial, and technology hub, Taipei has been at the center of rapid economic development in the country and has now become one of the global cities in technology and electronics.^[\[61\]](#cite_note-64)^ This development is part of the so-called [Taiwan Economic Miracle](/wiki/Taiwan_Economic_Miracle "Taiwan Economic Miracle") which has seen dramatic growth in the city following [foreign direct investment](/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment "Foreign direct investment") in the 1960s. Taiwan is now a [creditor](/wiki/Creditor "Creditor") economy, holding one of the world's largest [foreign exchange reserves](/wiki/List_of_countries_by_foreign_exchange_reserves "List of countries by foreign exchange reserves") of over US$403 billion as of December 2012.^[\[62\]](#cite_note-65)^{#cite_ref-65}

Despite the [Asian financial crisis](/wiki/1997_Asian_Financial_Crisis "1997 Asian Financial Crisis"), the economy continues to expand at about 5% per year, with virtually full employment and low inflation. The city's GDP stand at US$327 billion in 2014.^[\[63\]](#cite_note-66)^ As of 2013^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit)^, the nominal GDP per capita in Taipei city is 5th highest in East Asia, behind Tokyo, Singapore, Osaka, and Hong Kong, but ahead of Seoul, as well as London and Paris, according to *The Economist* .^[\[64\]](#cite_note-67)^ GDP per capita based on Purchasing Power Parity (PPP) in Taipei in 2015 was US$44,173, behind that of Singapore (US$90,151 in 2016 from the IMF) and Hong Kong (US$58,322 in 2016 from the IMF; also based on PPP).^[\[65\]](#cite_note-68)^ The *Financial Times* ranked Taipei highly in economic potential (2nd, behind Tokyo) and business friendliness (4th) in 2015.^[\[66\]](#cite_note-69)^ The city is home to 30 billionaires, the 16th most in the world, ahead of many global cities such as Los Angeles and Sydney.^[\[67\]](#cite_note-70)^ Business Insider also ranks Taipei the 5th most high-tech city globally, the highest in Asia, in 2017.^[\[68\]](#cite_note-71)^ While the IESE Cities in Motion Index 2017 ranks Taipei as the smartest technology city globally.^[\[69\]](#cite_note-72)^{#cite_ref-72}

Taipei's main development fields include the [information and communications technology](/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology "Information and communications technology") (hardware and software), biotechnology, general merchandizing (wholesale/retail), financial services, and [MICE](/wiki/Meetings,_incentives,_conferencing,_exhibitions "Meetings, incentives, conferencing, exhibitions") industries. Most of the country's major firms are based there including [Acer Computers](/wiki/Acer_Inc. "Acer Inc."), [Asus](/wiki/Asus "Asus"), [CTBC Bank](/wiki/CTBC_Bank "CTBC Bank"), [Fubon Financial Holding](/wiki/Fubon_Financial_Holding_Co. "Fubon Financial Holding Co."), [Tatung Company](/wiki/Tatung_Company "Tatung Company"), [D-Link](/wiki/D-Link "D-Link"), and others. 5 Global Fortune 500 companies are headquartered in Taipei.^[\[70\]](#cite_note-73)^ The city also attracts many multi-national corporations, international financial institutions, foreign consulates, and business organizations to set up base there. Thus, Taipei has nearly 3,500 registered foreign businesses and attracts over 50% of the total foreign investment in Taiwan.^[\[71\]](#cite_note-74)^ Foreign companies with offices or regional headquarters in Taipei include [Google](/wiki/Google "Google"), [Microsoft](/wiki/Microsoft "Microsoft"), [IBM](/wiki/IBM "IBM"), [Intel](/wiki/Intel "Intel"), [HSBC](/wiki/HSBC "HSBC"), [Citibank](/wiki/Citibank "Citibank"), [Facebook](/wiki/Facebook "Facebook"), [Amazon](/wiki/Amazon.com "Amazon.com"), [Apple](/wiki/Apple_Inc. "Apple Inc."), [JP Morgan](/wiki/JP_Morgan "JP Morgan"), [PwC](/wiki/PwC "PwC"), and many others. Most financial and foreign firms like to reside in the central business district of Taipei, the [Xinyi Special District](/wiki/Xinyi_Special_District "Xinyi Special District"): Citi, JP Morgan, DBS Bank, Cathay Life Insurance, Shin Kong Commercial Bank, and Hua Nan Bank have all established skyscrapers in the area. Meanwhile, technology and electronics companies are often co-located in the [Neihu Technology Park](/wiki/Neihu_Technology_Park "Neihu Technology Park") or the [Nankang Software Park](/wiki/Nankang_Software_Park "Nankang Software Park"). The startup and innovation scene in Taipei is also very vibrant. In 2018 alone, Microsoft announced plans to invest US$34 million to create an artificial intelligence R\&D center in Taipei, while Google announced it will hire 300 people and train 5,000 more in artificial intelligence for machines.^[\[72\]](#cite_note-75)^ Taipei is Google's biggest engineering site in Asia.^[\[73\]](#cite_note-76)^ IBM also announced in 2018 that it will develop a cloud research lab and expand its R\&D center in Taipei with eyes on artificial intelligence, blockchain technology, and cloud computing. According to the 2016 Global Entrepreneurship Development Index, Taipei's entrepreneurial spirit ranks 6th worldwide and 1st in Asia.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-77)^ Taipei has more than 400 startups and numerous incubation centers, accelerators, venture capitals, and angel investors.^[\[75\]](#cite_note-78)^ The city's startup ecosystem is valued at US$580 million by Startup Genome in 2018.^[\[76\]](#cite_note-79)^{#cite_ref-79}

Tourism is a small but significant component of the local economy^[\[77\]](#cite_note-80)^^[\[78\]](#cite_note-81)^ with international visitors totaling almost 3 million in 2008.^[\[79\]](#cite_note-82)^ Taipei has many top tourist attractions and contributes a significant amount to the US$6.8 billion tourism industry in Taiwan.^[\[80\]](#cite_note-83)^{#cite_ref-83}  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Culture")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei_city%27s_west_side_facing_the_Tamsui_River.jpg/220px-Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei_city%27s_west_side_facing_the_Tamsui_River.jpg)](/wiki/File:Aerial_panorama_of_Taipei_city%27s_west_side_facing_the_Tamsui_River.jpg) Aerial panorama of Taipei city facing the Tamsui River  

### Tourism {#Tourism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Tourism")\]  
See also: [List of tourist attractions in Taipei](/wiki/List_of_tourist_attractions_in_Taipei "List of tourist attractions in Taipei")

Tourism is a major part of Taipei's economy. In 2013, over 6.3 million overseas visitors visited Taipei, making the city the 15th most visited globally.^[\[81\]](#cite_note-84)^ The influx of visitors contributed US$10.8 billion to the city's economy in 2013, the 9th highest in the world and the most of any city in the Chinese-speaking world.^[\[82\]](#cite_note-85)^{#cite_ref-85}  

#### Commemorative sites and museums {#Commemorative_sites_and_museums}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Commemorative sites and museums")\]  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/CKS_Panorama.jpg/1000px-CKS_Panorama.jpg)](/wiki/File:CKS_Panorama.jpg "A panorama of the Liberty Square looking east, with the National Concert Hall (left) and the National Theater (right)")  
[](/wiki/File:CKS_Panorama.jpg "File:CKS Panorama.jpg")
A panorama of the [Liberty Square](/wiki/Liberty_Square_(Taipei) "Liberty Square (Taipei)") looking east, with the National Concert Hall (left) and the National Theater (right)
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg/220px-National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg)](/wiki/File:National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg) The [National Palace Museum](/wiki/National_Palace_Museum "National Palace Museum") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Taipei_228_Memorial_Museum_face_20070928.jpg/220px-Taipei_228_Memorial_Museum_face_20070928.jpg)](/wiki/File:Taipei_228_Memorial_Museum_face_20070928.jpg) The 228 Memorial Museum [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%B4%80%E5%B7%9E%E5%BA%B5.jpg/220px-%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%B4%80%E5%B7%9E%E5%BA%B5.jpg)](/wiki/File:%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%B4%80%E5%B7%9E%E5%BA%B5.jpg) Kishu An Forest of Literature [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/National_Concert_Hall_at_night_2013.jpg/220px-National_Concert_Hall_at_night_2013.jpg)](/wiki/File:National_Concert_Hall_at_night_2013.jpg) The [National Concert Hall](/wiki/National_Concert_Hall_(Taiwan) "National Concert Hall (Taiwan)") illuminated at night

The [National Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall](/wiki/National_Chiang_Kai-shek_Memorial_Hall "National Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall") is a monument, landmark and tourist attraction that was erected in memory of General [Chiang Kai-shek](/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek"), former [President of the Republic of China](/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China "President of the Republic of China").^[\[83\]](#cite_note-86)^ The structure stands at the east end of Memorial Hall Square, site of the [National Concert Hall](/wiki/National_Concert_Hall_(Taiwan) "National Concert Hall (Taiwan)") and [National Theater](/wiki/National_Theatre_(Taiwan) "National Theatre (Taiwan)") and their adjacent parks as well as the memorial. The landmarks of Liberty Square stand within sight of Taiwan's [Presidential Office Building](/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building_(Republic_of_China) "Presidential Office Building (Republic of China)") in Taipei's [Zhongzheng District](/wiki/Zhongzheng_District "Zhongzheng District").{#cite_ref-86}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/National_Taiwan_Museum_front_20070912.jpg/220px-National_Taiwan_Museum_front_20070912.jpg)](/wiki/File:National_Taiwan_Museum_front_20070912.jpg) The [National Taiwan Museum](/wiki/National_Taiwan_Museum "National Taiwan Museum")

The [National Taiwan Museum](/wiki/National_Taiwan_Museum "National Taiwan Museum") sits nearby in what is now [228 Peace Memorial Park](/wiki/228_Peace_Memorial_Park "228 Peace Memorial Park") and has worn its present name since 1999. The museum is [Taiwan](/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan")'s oldest, founded on 24 October 1908 by Taiwan's [Japanese colonial government](/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule "Taiwan under Japanese rule") (1895--1945) as the Taiwan Governor's Museum. It was launched with a collection of 10,000 items to celebrate the opening of the island's North--South Railway.^[\[84\]](#cite_note-ntminfo-87)^ In 1915 a new museum building opened its doors in what is now [228 Peace Memorial Park](/wiki/228_Peace_Memorial_Park "228 Peace Memorial Park"). This structure and the adjacent governor's office (now [Presidential Office Building](/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building_(Republic_of_China) "Presidential Office Building (Republic of China)")), served as the two most recognizable public buildings in Taiwan during its period of [Japanese rule](/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule "Taiwan under Japanese rule").^[\[84\]](#cite_note-ntminfo-87)^{#cite_ref-ntminfo_87-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_20190629.jpg/220px-Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_20190629.jpg)](/wiki/File:Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_20190629.jpg) [Shung Ye Museum of Formosan Aborigines](/wiki/Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines "Shung Ye Museum of Formosan Aborigines")

The [National Palace Museum](/wiki/National_Palace_Museum "National Palace Museum") is a vast [art gallery](/wiki/Art_gallery "Art gallery") and [museum](/wiki/Museum "Museum") built around a permanent collection centered on [ancient Chinese artifacts](/wiki/Ancient_China "Ancient China"). It should not be confused with the [Palace Museum](/wiki/Forbidden_City "Forbidden City") in [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing") (which it is named after); both institutions trace their origins to the same institution. The collections were divided in the 1940s as a result of the [Chinese Civil War](/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War "Chinese Civil War").^[\[85\]](#cite_note-88)^^[\[86\]](#cite_note-npmwashpo-89)^ The National Palace Museum in Taipei now boasts a truly international collection while housing one of the world's largest collections of artifacts from ancient China.^[\[86\]](#cite_note-npmwashpo-89)^{#cite_ref-npmwashpo_89-1}

The [Shung Ye Museum of Formosan Aborigines](/wiki/Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines "Shung Ye Museum of Formosan Aborigines") stands just 200 m (660 ft) across the road from the National Palace Museum. The museum offers displays of art and historical items by [Taiwanese aborigines](/wiki/Taiwanese_aborigines "Taiwanese aborigines") along with a range of multimedia displays.

The [Taipei Fine Arts Museum](/wiki/Taipei_Fine_Arts_Museum "Taipei Fine Arts Museum") was established in 1983 as the first museum in Taiwan dedicated to [modern art](/wiki/Modern_art "Modern art"). The museum is housed in a building designed for the purpose that takes inspiration from Japanese designs. Most art in the collection is by [Taiwanese](/wiki/Taiwanese_people "Taiwanese people") artists since 1940. Over 3,000 art works are organized into 13 groups.

The [National Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall](/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Memorial_Hall "Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall") near [Taipei 101](/wiki/Taipei_101 "Taipei 101") in [Xinyi District](/wiki/Xinyi_District,_Taipei "Xinyi District, Taipei") is named in honor of a founding father of the [Republic of China](/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349) "Republic of China (1912–49)"), [Sun Yat-sen](/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen "Sun Yat-sen"). The hall, completed on 16 May 1972, originally featured exhibits that depicted revolutionary events in the [Republican period of China](/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912-1949) "Republic of China (1912-1949)"). Today it functions as multi-purpose [social](/wiki/Social_center "Social center"), [educational](/wiki/Educational "Educational"), [concert](/wiki/Concert "Concert") and [cultural](/wiki/Cultural "Cultural") center for Taiwan's citizens.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-90)^{#cite_ref-90}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG/220px-%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG)](/wiki/File:%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG) [Museum of Contemporary Art Taipei](/wiki/MoCA_Taipei "MoCA Taipei"), also known as "old city hall"

In 2001 a new museum opened as [Museum of Contemporary Art Taipei](/wiki/MoCA_Taipei "MoCA Taipei"). The museum is housed in a building that formerly housed Taipei City government offices.^[\[88\]](#cite_note-tfaminfo-91)^{#cite_ref-tfaminfo_91-0}  

#### Taipei 101 {#Taipei_101}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Taipei 101")\]

[Taipei 101](/wiki/Taipei_101 "Taipei 101") is a 101-floor [landmark](/wiki/Landmark "Landmark") [skyscraper](/wiki/Skyscraper "Skyscraper") that claimed the title of [world's tallest building](/wiki/World%27s_tallest_structures "World's tallest structures") when it opened in 2004, a title it held for six years before the [Burj Khalifa](/wiki/Burj_Khalifa "Burj Khalifa") in [Dubai](/wiki/Dubai "Dubai") was completed. Designed by [C.Y. Lee \& Partners](/wiki/C.Y._Lee_%26_Partners "C.Y. Lee & Partners") and constructed by [KTRT Joint Venture](/wiki/KTRT_Joint_Venture "KTRT Joint Venture"), Taipei 101 measures 509 m (1,670 ft) from ground to top, making it the first skyscraper in the world to break the half-kilometer mark in height. Built to withstand typhoon winds and earthquake tremors, its design incorporates many engineering innovations and has won numerous international awards. Today, the Taipei 101 remains one of the tallest skyscrapers in the world and holds [LEED](/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design "Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design")'s certification as the world's largest "green" building. Its shopping mall and its indoor and outdoor observatories draws visitors from all over the world. Taipei 101's [New Year's Eve](/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve "New Year's Eve") fireworks display is a regular feature of international broadcasts.  

#### Performing arts {#Performing_arts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Performing arts")\]

The [National Theater and Concert Hall](/wiki/National_Theater_and_Concert_Hall "National Theater and Concert Hall") stand at Taipei's [Liberty Square](/wiki/Liberty_Square_(Taipei) "Liberty Square (Taipei)") and host events by foreign and domestic performers. Other leading concert venues include [Zhongshan Hall](/wiki/Zhongshan_Hall "Zhongshan Hall") at [Ximending](/wiki/Ximending "Ximending") and the [Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall](/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Memorial_Hall "Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall") near [Taipei 101](/wiki/Taipei_101 "Taipei 101").

A new venue, the [Taipei Performing Arts Center](/wiki/Taipei_Performing_Arts_Center "Taipei Performing Arts Center") opened in 2022.^[\[89\]](#cite_note-92)^^[\[90\]](#cite_note-93)^ The venue is near the [Shilin Night Market](/wiki/Shilin_Night_Market "Shilin Night Market")^[\[91\]](#cite_note-94)^ and houses three theaters for events with multi-week runs. The architectural design, by [Rem Koolhaas](/wiki/Rem_Koolhaas "Rem Koolhaas") and [OMA](/wiki/Office_for_Metropolitan_Architecture "Office for Metropolitan Architecture"), was determined in 2009 in an international competition.^[\[92\]](#cite_note-95)^ The same design process is also in place for a new [Taipei Center for Popular Music](/wiki/Taipei_Center_for_Popular_Music "Taipei Center for Popular Music") and [Taipei City Museum](/wiki/Taipei_City_Museum "Taipei City Museum").^[\[93\]](#cite_note-96)^{#cite_ref-96}  

#### Shopping and recreation {#Shopping_and_recreation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Shopping and recreation")\]  
Main article: [Shopping in Taipei](/wiki/Shopping_in_Taipei "Shopping in Taipei")

Taipei is known for its many [night markets](/wiki/Night_markets_in_Taiwan "Night markets in Taiwan"), which include the [Shilin Night Market](/wiki/Shilin_Night_Market "Shilin Night Market") in the [Shilin District](/wiki/Shilin_District "Shilin District"). The surrounding streets by Shilin Night Market are extremely crowded during the evening, usually opening late afternoon and operating well past midnight. Most night markets feature individual stalls selling a mixture of food, clothing, and consumer goods.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Central_Pictures_New_World_Building_night_20061222.jpg/220px-Central_Pictures_New_World_Building_night_20061222.jpg)](/wiki/File:Central_Pictures_New_World_Building_night_20061222.jpg) The busy streets of [Ximending](/wiki/Ximending "Ximending") at night

[Ximending](/wiki/Ximending "Ximending") has been an area for shopping and entertainment since the 1930s. Historic structures include a concert hall, a historic cinema, and the [Red House Theater](/wiki/Red_House_Theater "Red House Theater"). Modern structures house karaoke businesses, art film cinemas, wide-release movie cinemas, electronic stores, and a wide variety of restaurants and fashion clothing stores.^[\[94\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly200799-97)^ The pedestrian area is especially popular with teens and has been called the "[Harajuku](/wiki/Harajuku "Harajuku")" of Taipei.^[\[95\]](#cite_note-98)^{#cite_ref-98}

The newly developed [Xinyi District](/wiki/Xinyi_District,_Taipei "Xinyi District, Taipei") is popular with tourists and locals alike for its many entertainment and shopping venues, as well as being the home of [Taipei 101](/wiki/Taipei_101 "Taipei 101"), a prime tourist attraction. Malls in the area include the sprawling [Shin Kong Mitsukoshi](/wiki/Mitsukoshi "Mitsukoshi") complex, Breeze Center, Bellavita, Taipei 101 mall, [Eslite Bookstore](/wiki/Eslite_Bookstore "Eslite Bookstore")'s flagship store (which includes a boutique mall), The Living Mall, ATT shopping mall, and the Vieshow Cinemas (formerly known as Warner Village). The Xinyi district also serves as the center of Taipei's active nightlife, with several popular lounge bars and nightclubs concentrated in a relatively small area around the Neo19, ATT 4 FUN and Taipei 101 buildings.

The thriving shopping area around [Taipei Main Station](/wiki/Taipei_Main_Station "Taipei Main Station") includes the [Taipei Underground Market](/wiki/Taipei_Underground_Market "Taipei Underground Market") and the original Shin Kong [Mitsukoshi](/wiki/Mitsukoshi "Mitsukoshi") department store at [Shin Kong Life Tower](/wiki/Shin_Kong_Life_Tower "Shin Kong Life Tower"). Other popular shopping destinations include the [Zhongshan Metro Mall](/wiki/Zhongshan_Metro_Mall "Zhongshan Metro Mall"), [Dihua Street](/wiki/Dihua_Street "Dihua Street") and the [Guang Hua Digital Plaza](/wiki/Guang_Hua_Digital_Plaza "Guang Hua Digital Plaza"). The [Miramar Entertainment Park](/wiki/Miramar_Entertainment_Park "Miramar Entertainment Park") is known for its large Ferris wheel and [IMAX](/wiki/IMAX "IMAX") theater.

Taipei maintains an extensive system of parks, green spaces, and nature preserves. Parks and forestry areas of note in and around the city include [Yangmingshan National Park](/wiki/Yangmingshan_National_Park "Yangmingshan National Park"), [Taipei Zoo](/wiki/Taipei_Zoo "Taipei Zoo") and [Da-an Forest Park](/wiki/Daan_Forest_Park "Daan Forest Park"). Located 10 km (6.2 mi) north of the city center, [Yangmingshan National Park](/wiki/Yangmingshan_National_Park "Yangmingshan National Park") is visited for its cherry blossoms, [hot springs](/wiki/Hot_springs "Hot springs"), and sulfur deposits. It is the home of writer [Lin Yutang](/wiki/Lin_Yutang "Lin Yutang"), the summer residence of [Chiang Kai-shek](/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek"), residences of foreign diplomats, the [Chinese Culture University](/wiki/Chinese_Culture_University "Chinese Culture University"), the meeting place of the now defunct [National Assembly of the Republic of China](/wiki/National_Assembly_of_the_Republic_of_China "National Assembly of the Republic of China"), and the [Kuomintang](/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang") Party Archives. The [Taipei Zoo](/wiki/Taipei_Zoo "Taipei Zoo") was founded in 1914 and covers an area of 165 hectares for animal sanctuary.

[Bitan](/wiki/Bitan "Bitan") is known for boating and water sports. [Tamsui](/wiki/Tamsui_District "Tamsui District") is a popular sea-side resort town. Ocean beaches are accessible in several directions from Taipei.  

#### Temples {#Temples}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Temples")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg/220px-Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg)](/wiki/File:Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg) Built in 1738, [Bangka Lungshan Temple](/wiki/Lungshan_Temple_(Taipei) "Lungshan Temple (Taipei)") is one of the oldest temples in the city.

Taipei has a variety of temples dedicating to Deities from [Chinese folk religion](/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion "Chinese folk religion"), [Taoism](/wiki/Taoism "Taoism") and [Chinese Buddhism](/wiki/Chinese_Buddhism "Chinese Buddhism"). The [Bangka Lungshan Temple](/wiki/Lungshan_Temple_(Taipei) "Lungshan Temple (Taipei)") (艋舺龍山寺), built in 1738 and located in the [Wanhua District](/wiki/Wanhua_District "Wanhua District"), demonstrates an example of architecture with southern [Chinese influences](/wiki/Chinese_architecture "Chinese architecture") commonly seen on older buildings in Taiwan. [Qingshui Temple](/wiki/Bangka_Qingshui_Temple "Bangka Qingshui Temple") (艋舺清水巖) built in 1787 and Qingshan Temple (艋舺青山宮) together with Lungshan Temple are the three most prominent landmark temples in Bangka or Wanhua District.

Other temples include [Baoan Temple](/wiki/Dalongdong_Baoan_Temple "Dalongdong Baoan Temple") (大龍峒保安宮) located in historic [Dalongdong](/wiki/Dalongdong "Dalongdong"), a national historical site, and [Xia Hai City God Temple](/wiki/Taipei_Xia-Hai_City_God_Temple "Taipei Xia-Hai City God Temple") (大稻埕霞海城隍廟), located in the old [Dadaocheng](/wiki/Twatutia "Twatutia") community, constructed with architecture similar to temples in southern [Fujian](/wiki/Fujian "Fujian").^[\[96\]](#cite_note-temples-99)^ The [Taipei Confucius Temple](/wiki/Taipei_Confucius_Temple "Taipei Confucius Temple") (臺北孔子廟) traces its history back to 1879 during the [Qing dynasty](/wiki/Qing_dynasty "Qing dynasty") and also incorporates southern Fujian-style architecture.^[\[97\]](#cite_note-100)^ [Ciyou Temple](/wiki/Ciyou_Temple "Ciyou Temple") (松山慈祐宮) in Songshan District, [Guandu Temple](/wiki/Guandu_Temple "Guandu Temple") (關渡宮) in Beitou District, [Hsing Tian Kong](/wiki/Hsing_Tian_Kong "Hsing Tian Kong") (行天宮) in Zhongshan District and [Zhinan Temple](/wiki/Zhinan_Temple "Zhinan Temple") (指南宮) in Wenshan District are also popular temples for locals and tourists. [Xinsheng South Road](/wiki/Xinsheng_Road "Xinsheng Road") is known as the "Road to Heaven" due to its high concentration of temples, churches, and other houses of worship.^[\[98\]](#cite_note-101)^^[\[99\]](#cite_note-102)^{#cite_ref-102}

The [Shandao Temple](/wiki/Shandao_Temple "Shandao Temple") (善導寺) built in 1929 and located in Zhongzheng District, is the largest Buddhist temple in Taipei. [Fo Guang Shan](/wiki/Fo_Guang_Shan "Fo Guang Shan") has a modern temple known as Fo Guang Shan Taipei Vihara (佛光山臺北道場) in Xinyi District, while [Dharma Drum Mountain](/wiki/Dharma_Drum_Mountain "Dharma Drum Mountain") owns the Degui Academy (德貴學苑), an education center in Zhongzheng District and the [Nung Chan Monastery](/wiki/Nung_Chan_Monastery "Nung Chan Monastery") (農禪寺) in Beitou District. [Linji Huguo Chan Temple](/wiki/Linji_Huguo_Chan_Temple "Linji Huguo Chan Temple") (臨濟護國禪寺) in Zhongshan District was commenced in 1900 and completed in 1911, it is one of the very few Japanese style Buddhist Temples that was well-preserved in Taiwan.

Besides large temples, small outdoor shrines to local deities are very common and are commonly found next to roads as well as in parks and neighborhoods. Many homes and businesses may also set up small shrines of candles, figurines, and offerings. Some restaurants, for example, may set up a small shrine to the [Kitchen God](/wiki/Kitchen_God "Kitchen God") for success in a restaurant business.^[\[100\]](#cite_note-103)^{#cite_ref-103}  

### Festivals and events {#Festivals_and_events}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Festivals and events")\]

Many yearly festivals are held in Taipei. In recent years some festivals, such as the Double Ten Day fireworks and concerts, are increasingly hosted on a rotating basis by a number of cities around Taiwan.

When [New Year's Eve](/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve "New Year's Eve") arrives on the [solar calendar](/wiki/Solar_calendar "Solar calendar"), thousands of people converge on Taipei's [Xinyi District](/wiki/Xinyi_District,_Taipei "Xinyi District, Taipei") for [parades](/wiki/Parade "Parade"), outdoor [concerts](/wiki/Concerts "Concerts") by [popular artists](/wiki/Mandopop "Mandopop"), [street shows](/wiki/Street_performer "Street performer"), round-the clock [nightlife](/wiki/Nightlife "Nightlife"). The high point is the countdown to midnight, when [Taipei 101](/wiki/Taipei_101 "Taipei 101") assumes the role of the world's largest [fireworks](/wiki/Fireworks "Fireworks") platform.^[\[101\]](#cite_note-104)^{#cite_ref-104}

The Taipei [Lantern Festival](/wiki/Lantern_Festival "Lantern Festival") concludes the [Lunar New Year](/wiki/Lunar_New_Year "Lunar New Year") holiday. The timing of the city's lantern exhibit coincides with the national festival in [Pingxi](/wiki/Pingxi,_Taipei "Pingxi, Taipei"), when thousands of fire lanterns are released into the sky.^[\[102\]](#cite_note-tourism-105)^ The city's lantern exhibit rotates among different downtown locales from year to year, including [Liberty Square](/wiki/Liberty_Square_(Taipei) "Liberty Square (Taipei)"), [Taipei 101](/wiki/Taipei_101 "Taipei 101"), and [Zhongshan Hall](/wiki/Zhongshan_Hall "Zhongshan Hall") in [Ximending](/wiki/Ximending "Ximending").{#cite_ref-tourism_105-0}

On [Double Ten Day](/wiki/Double_Ten_Day "Double Ten Day"), patriotic celebrations are held in front of the [Presidential Office Building](/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building_(Republic_of_China) "Presidential Office Building (Republic of China)"). Other annual festivals include [Ancestors Day (Tomb-Sweeping Day)](/wiki/Qingming_Festival "Qingming Festival"), the [Dragon Boat Festival](/wiki/Duanwu_Festival "Duanwu Festival"), the [Zhong Yuan Festival](/wiki/Zhong_Yuan_Festival "Zhong Yuan Festival"), and the [Mid-Autumn Festival (Mooncake Festival)](/wiki/Mid-Autumn_Festival "Mid-Autumn Festival").^[\[102\]](#cite_note-tourism-105)^ [Qing Shan King Sacrificial Ceremony](/wiki/Qing_Shan_King_Sacrificial_Ceremony "Qing Shan King Sacrificial Ceremony") (青山王祭) is a century-old grand festival that is held annually in [Wanhua District](/wiki/Wanhua_District "Wanhua District").{#cite_ref-tourism_105-1}

Taipei regularly hosts its share of international events. The city recently hosted the 2009 [Summer Deaflympics](/wiki/Summer_Deaflympics "Summer Deaflympics").^[\[103\]](#cite_note-106)^ This event was followed by the [Taipei International Flora Exposition](/wiki/Taipei_International_Flora_Exposition "Taipei International Flora Exposition"), a [garden festival](/wiki/Garden_festival "Garden festival") hosted from November 2010 to April 2011. The Floral Expo was the first of its kind to take place in Taiwan and only the seventh hosted in [Asia](/wiki/Asia "Asia"); the expo admitted 110,000 visitors on 27 February 2011.{#cite_ref-106}  

Government {#Government}
------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Government")\]  
Main articles: [Taipei City Government](/wiki/Taipei_City_Government "Taipei City Government") and [Taipei City Council](/wiki/Taipei_City_Council "Taipei City Council")  
See also: [Mayor of Taipei City](/wiki/Mayor_of_Taipei_City "Mayor of Taipei City") and [Republic of China municipal elections, 2010](/wiki/Republic_of_China_municipal_elections,_2010 "Republic of China municipal elections, 2010")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Taipei_City_Hall_front_view_20050110.jpg/220px-Taipei_City_Hall_front_view_20050110.jpg)](/wiki/File:Taipei_City_Hall_front_view_20050110.jpg) [Taipei City Government](/wiki/Taipei_City_Government "Taipei City Government") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%82%E8%AD%B0%E6%9C%83.JPG/220px-%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%82%E8%AD%B0%E6%9C%83.JPG)](/wiki/File:%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%82%E8%AD%B0%E6%9C%83.JPG) [Taipei City Council](/wiki/Taipei_City_Council "Taipei City Council")

Taipei City is a [special municipality](/wiki/Special_municipality_of_Taiwan "Special municipality of Taiwan") which is directly under the [Executive Yuan](/wiki/Executive_Yuan "Executive Yuan") ([Central Government](/wiki/Central_Government "Central Government")). The [mayor of Taipei City](/wiki/Mayor_of_Taipei "Mayor of Taipei") was an appointed position since Taipei's conversion to a centrally administered municipality in 1967 until the first public election was held in 1994.^[\[104\]](#cite_note-107)^ The position has a four-year term and is elected by direct popular vote. The first elected mayor was [Chen Shui-bian](/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian "Chen Shui-bian") of the [Democratic Progressive Party](/wiki/Democratic_Progressive_Party "Democratic Progressive Party"). [Ma Ying-jeou](/wiki/Ma_Ying-jeou "Ma Ying-jeou") took office in 1998 for two terms, before handing it over to [Hau Lung-pin](/wiki/Hau_Lung-pin "Hau Lung-pin") who won the 2006 mayoral election on 9 December 2006.^[\[105\]](#cite_note-108)^ Both Chen Shui-bian and Ma Ying-Jeou went on to become [President of the Republic of China](/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China "President of the Republic of China"). The incumbent mayor, [Chiang Wan-an](/wiki/Chiang_Wan-an "Chiang Wan-an") of [Kuomintang](/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang"), took office on 25 December 2022.{#cite_ref-108}

Based on the outcomes of previous elections in the past decade, the vote of the overall constituency of Taipei City shows a slight inclination towards the pro-KMT camp (the [Pan-Blue Coalition](/wiki/Pan-Blue_Coalition "Pan-Blue Coalition"));^[\[106\]](#cite_note-109)^ however, the pro-DPP camp (the [Pan-Green Coalition](/wiki/Pan-Green_Coalition "Pan-Green Coalition")) also has considerable support.^[\[107\]](#cite_note-110)^{#cite_ref-110}

[Ketagalan Boulevard](/wiki/Ketagalan_Boulevard "Ketagalan Boulevard"), where the [Presidential Office Building](/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building_(Republic_of_China) "Presidential Office Building (Republic of China)") and other government structures are situated, is often the site of mass gatherings such as inauguration and national holiday parades, receptions for visiting dignitaries, political demonstrations,^[\[108\]](#cite_note-111)^^[\[109\]](#cite_note-112)^ and public festivals.^[\[110\]](#cite_note-113)^{#cite_ref-113}  

### Garbage recycling {#Garbage_recycling}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Garbage recycling")\]

Taipei City strongly promotes garbage recycling, with such success that other countries have sent teams to study the recycling system. After the [Environmental Protection Administration](/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Administration_(Republic_of_China) "Environmental Protection Administration (Republic of China)") (EPA) established a program in 1998 combining the efforts of communities, a financial resource named the Recycling Fund was made available to recycling companies and waste collectors. The EPA also introduced garbage recycling trucks, in effort to raise community recycling awareness, that broadcast classical music (specifically Beethoven's "Für Elise" and Tekla Bądarzewska-Baranowska's "A Maiden's Prayer") to announce its arrival to the community.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-114)^ Manufacturers, vendors and importers of recyclable waste pay fees to the Fund, which uses the money to set firm prices for recyclables and subsidize local recycling efforts. Between 1998 and 2008, the recycling rate increased from 6 percent to 32 percent.^[\[112\]](#cite_note-115)^ This improvement enabled the government of Taipei to demonstrate its recycling system to the world at the [Shanghai World Expo 2010](/wiki/Expo_2010 "Expo 2010").{#cite_ref-115}  

### Administrative divisions {#Administrative_divisions}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Administrative divisions")\]

Taipei City is divided up into 12 administrative [districts](/wiki/District_(ROC) "District (ROC)") (區; *qū* ).^[\[113\]](#cite_note-116)^ Each district is further divided up into [urban villages](/wiki/Village_(Taiwan) "Village (Taiwan)") (里), which are further sub-divided up into neighborhoods (鄰). [Xinyi District](/wiki/Xinyi_District,_Taipei "Xinyi District, Taipei") is the seat of the municipality where the [Taipei City Government](/wiki/Taipei_City_Government "Taipei City Government") headquarters is located.{#cite_ref-116}
{#cite_ref-govtp_118-0}
