### City planning {#City_planning}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: City planning")\]

The city is characterized by straight roads and public buildings of grand Western architectural styles.^[\[116\]](#cite_note-jones-119)^ The city is built on a square grid configuration; however, these blocks are huge by international standards with 500 m (1,640.42 ft) sides. The area in between these blocks is infilled with lanes and alleys, which provide access to quieter residential or mixed-use development. Other than a citywide 30 km/h (19 mph) speed limit, there is little uniform planning within this "hidden" area; therefore, lanes (perpendicular to streets) and alleys (parallel with streets, or, conceptually, perpendicular to lanes) spill out from the main [controlled-access highways](/wiki/Controlled-access_highway "Controlled-access highway"). These minor roads are not always perpendicular and sometimes cut through the block diagonally.{#cite_ref-jones_119-0}

Although development began in the western districts of the city (still considered the cultural heart of Taipei) due to trade, the eastern districts have become the focus of recent development projects. Many of the western districts have become targets of [urban renewal](/wiki/Urban_renewal "Urban renewal") initiatives.^[\[116\]](#cite_note-jones-119)^{#cite_ref-jones_119-1}  

Transportation {#Transportation}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Transportation")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Nangang_Exhibition_Center_metro_Line_5.jpg/220px-Nangang_Exhibition_Center_metro_Line_5.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nangang_Exhibition_Center_metro_Line_5.jpg) Underground platforms of [Nangang Exhibition Center](/wiki/Taipei_Nangang_Exhibition_Center_Station "Taipei Nangang Exhibition Center Station") Station on the [Taipei Metro](/wiki/Taipei_Metro "Taipei Metro") system

[Public transport](/wiki/Public_transport "Public transport") accounts for a substantial portion of transportation trips in Taipei. According to a 2022 government survey, 34.9% of transportation trips were taken on public transit in Taipei, higher than any other locality in the country.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-2022MOTCsurvey-120)^ [Private transport](/wiki/Private_transport "Private transport") consists of [motor scooters](/wiki/Scooter_(motorcycle) "Scooter (motorcycle)"), private cars, taxi cabs and [bicycles](/wiki/Bicycle "Bicycle"). Private transport trips represented 41.6% of trips taken in Taipei in 2022, the lowest in Taiwan.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-2022MOTCsurvey-120)^{#cite_ref-2022MOTCsurvey_120-1}

[Taipei Main Station](/wiki/Taipei_Main_Station "Taipei Main Station") serves as the comprehensive hub for the subway, bus, conventional rail, and high-speed rail.^[\[118\]](#cite_note-tpctoday-121)^ A [contactless smartcard](/wiki/Contactless_smart_card "Contactless smart card"), known as [EasyCard](/wiki/EasyCard "EasyCard"), can be used for all modes of public transit as well as several retail outlets. It contains credits that are deducted each time a ride is taken.^[\[119\]](#cite_note-122)^ The EasyCard is read via [MIFARE](/wiki/MIFARE "MIFARE") panels on buses and in MRT stations, and it does not need to be removed from one's wallet or purse.{#cite_ref-122}  

### Metro {#Metro}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Metro")\]  
Main articles: [Taipei Metro](/wiki/Taipei_Metro "Taipei Metro") and [Taoyuan Airport MRT](/wiki/Taoyuan_Airport_MRT "Taoyuan Airport MRT")

Taipei's public transport system, the [Taipei Metro](/wiki/Taipei_Metro "Taipei Metro") (commonly referred to as the MRT), incorporates a [metro](/wiki/Rapid_transit "Rapid transit") and [light rail](/wiki/Light_rail "Light rail") system based on advanced [VAL](/wiki/V%C3%A9hicule_Automatique_L%C3%A9ger "Véhicule Automatique Léger") and [Bombardier](/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation "Bombardier Transportation") technology. There are currently six metro lines that are organized and labeled in three ways: by color, line number and depot station name. In addition to the rapid transit system itself, the Taipei Metro also includes several public facilities such as the [Maokong Gondola](/wiki/Maokong_Gondola "Maokong Gondola"), underground shopping malls, parks, and public squares. Modifications to existing [railway](/wiki/Taiwan_Railways_Administration "Taiwan Railways Administration") lines to integrate them into the metro system are underway.

In 2017 [a rapid transit line](/wiki/Taoyuan_Airport_MRT "Taoyuan Airport MRT") was opened to connect Taipei with [Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport](/wiki/Taiwan_Taoyuan_International_Airport "Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport") and [Zhongli District](/wiki/Zhongli_District "Zhongli District"). The new line is part of the new [Taoyuan Metro](/wiki/Taoyuan_Metro "Taoyuan Metro") system.

On 31 January 2020, Hitachi Rail Corporation officially commissioned Phase 1 of the [Circular line](/wiki/Circular_line_(New_Taipei_Metro) "Circular line (New Taipei Metro)") which took place at [Shisizhang station](/wiki/Shisizhang_station "Shisizhang station"). The Circular line is a 15.4 km driverless rail system. The Circular line offered free rides beginning in February 2020 for passengers to test the route.^[\[120\]](#cite_note-123)^^[\[121\]](#cite_note-124)^{#cite_ref-124}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/East_1_gate%2C_TRA_Taipei_Station_20081004.jpg/220px-East_1_gate%2C_TRA_Taipei_Station_20081004.jpg)](/wiki/File:East_1_gate,_TRA_Taipei_Station_20081004.jpg) Taipei Main Station front  

### Rail {#Rail}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Rail")\]  
Main articles: [Taiwan High Speed Rail](/wiki/Taiwan_High_Speed_Rail "Taiwan High Speed Rail") and [Taiwan Railways Administration](/wiki/Taiwan_Railways_Administration "Taiwan Railways Administration")

Beginning in 1983, surface rail lines in the city were moved underground as part of the [Taipei Railway Underground Project](/wiki/Taipei_Railway_Underground_Project "Taipei Railway Underground Project").^[\[122\]](#cite_note-125)^ The [Taiwan High Speed Rail](/wiki/Taiwan_High_Speed_Rail "Taiwan High Speed Rail") system opened in 2007. The bullet trains connect Taipei with the west coast cities of [New Taipei](/wiki/New_Taipei "New Taipei"), [Taoyuan](/wiki/Taoyuan_City "Taoyuan City"), [Hsinchu](/wiki/Hsinchu "Hsinchu"), [Taichung](/wiki/Taichung "Taichung"), [Chiayi](/wiki/Chiayi "Chiayi"), and [Tainan](/wiki/Tainan_City "Tainan City") before terminating at [Zuoying](/wiki/Zuoying_District "Zuoying District") ([Kaohsiung](/wiki/Kaohsiung "Kaohsiung")) at speeds that cut travel times by 60% or more from what they normally are on a bus or conventional train.^[\[123\]](#cite_note-126)^ The [Taiwan Railways Administration](/wiki/Taiwan_Railways_Administration "Taiwan Railways Administration") also runs passenger and freight services throughout the entire island.{#cite_ref-126}  

### Bus {#Bus}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Bus")\]  
Main article: [Taipei Joint Bus System](/wiki/Taipei_Joint_Bus_System "Taipei Joint Bus System")

An extensive [city bus system](/wiki/Taipei_bus "Taipei bus") serves metropolitan areas not covered by the metro, with exclusive bus lanes to facilitate transportation.^[\[118\]](#cite_note-tpctoday-121)^ Riders of the city metro system are able to use the EasyCard for discounted fares on buses, and vice versa. A unique feature of the Taipei bus system is the joint venture of private transportation companies that operate the system's routes while sharing the fare system. This route is in sharp contrast to bus systems in the U.S. which are mostly public entities. Several major intercity bus terminals are located throughout the city, including the [Taipei Bus Station](/wiki/Taipei_Bus_Station "Taipei Bus Station") and [Taipei City Hall Bus Station](/wiki/Taipei_City_Hall_Bus_Station "Taipei City Hall Bus Station").^[\[124\]](#cite_note-127)^{#cite_ref-127}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG/220px-Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG)](/wiki/File:Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG) Taipei Songshan Airport  

### Airports {#Airports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Airports")\]  
Main articles: [Taoyuan International Airport](/wiki/Taoyuan_International_Airport "Taoyuan International Airport") and [Songshan Airport](/wiki/Songshan_Airport "Songshan Airport")

Most scheduled international flights are served by [Taoyuan International Airport](/wiki/Taoyuan_International_Airport "Taoyuan International Airport") in nearby [Taoyuan City](/wiki/Taoyuan,_Taiwan "Taoyuan, Taiwan"). [Songshan Airport](/wiki/Songshan_Airport "Songshan Airport"), at the heart of the city in the [Songshan District](/wiki/Songshan_District,_Taipei "Songshan District, Taipei"), serves domestic flights and scheduled flights to [Haneda Airport](/wiki/Haneda_Airport "Haneda Airport") in [Tokyo](/wiki/Tokyo "Tokyo"), [Gimpo International Airport](/wiki/Gimpo_International_Airport "Gimpo International Airport") in [Seoul](/wiki/Seoul "Seoul"), and about 15 destinations in the [People's Republic of China](/wiki/China "China"). Songshan Airport is accessible by the Taipei Metro [Neihu Line](/wiki/Neihu_Line_(TRTS) "Neihu Line (TRTS)"); Taoyuan International Airport is accessible by the [Taoyuan Airport MRT](/wiki/Taoyuan_Airport_MRT "Taoyuan Airport MRT").  

### Ticketing {#Ticketing}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Ticketing")\]

In 1994, following the rapid development of Taipei, a white paper for transport policies expressed the strong objective of creating a transport system for the people of Taipei to accommodate the burgeoning city's needs. In 1999, they chose Mitac consortium, which Thales-Transportation Systems is part of. [Thales](/wiki/Thales_Group "Thales Group") was then selected again in 2005 to deploy an upgrade of Taipei's public transport network with an end-to-end and fully contactless automatic fare collection solution that integrates 116 metro stations, 5,000 buses and 92 car parks.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^  

Education {#Education}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Education")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%9D%A3%E5%BA%9C%E8%87%BA%E5%8C%97%E9%86%AB%E9%99%A2.jpg/220px-%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%9D%A3%E5%BA%9C%E8%87%BA%E5%8C%97%E9%86%AB%E9%99%A2.jpg)](/wiki/File:%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%9D%A3%E5%BA%9C%E8%87%BA%E5%8C%97%E9%86%AB%E9%99%A2.jpg) *West Site* of [National Taiwan University Hospital](/wiki/National_Taiwan_University_Hospital "National Taiwan University Hospital")

Taipei is home to the campuses of 24 universities and [Academia Sinica](/wiki/Academia_Sinica "Academia Sinica"), Taiwan's national academy which supports the Taiwan International Graduate Program:

Technology](/wiki/China_University_of_Technology "China University of Technology") (1965) |

[National Taiwan University](/wiki/National_Taiwan_University "National Taiwan University") (NTU or *Tai-Da* ) was established in 1928 during the period of Japanese colonial rule. NTU has produced many political and social leaders in Taiwan. Both [pan-blue](/wiki/Pan-blue_coalition "Pan-blue coalition") and [pan-green](/wiki/Pan-green_coalition "Pan-green coalition") movements in Taiwan are rooted on the NTU campus. The university has six campuses in the greater Taipei region (including [New Taipei](/wiki/New_Taipei "New Taipei")) and two additional campuses in [Nantou County](/wiki/Nantou_County "Nantou County"). The university governs farms, forests, and hospitals for educational and research purposes. The main campus is in Taipei's Da-An district, where most department buildings and all the administrative buildings are located. The College of Law and the College of Medicine are located near the [Presidential Office Building](/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building_(Republic_of_China) "Presidential Office Building (Republic of China)"). The [National Taiwan University Hospital](/wiki/National_Taiwan_University_Hospital "National Taiwan University Hospital") is a leading international center of medical research.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-128)^{#cite_ref-128}

[National Taiwan Normal University](/wiki/National_Taiwan_Normal_University "National Taiwan Normal University") (NTNU or *Shi-Da* ) likewise traces its origins to the Japanese colonial period. Founded as Taihoku College in 1922 and organized as a teacher training institution by the Kuomintang in 1946, NTNU has since developed into a comprehensive international university. The university boasts especially strong programs in the humanities and international education. Worldwide it is perhaps best known as home of the [Mandarin Training Center](/wiki/Mandarin_Training_Center "Mandarin Training Center"), a program that offers [Mandarin language](/wiki/Mandarin_language "Mandarin language") training each year to over a thousand students from scores of countries throughout the world. The main campus, in Taipei's Daan district near MRT Guting Station, is known for its historic architecture. The Shida market area surrounding this campus takes its name from the school's acronym.  

Sports {#Sports}
----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg/220px-Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg)](/wiki/File:Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg) [Taipei Arena](/wiki/Taipei_Arena "Taipei Arena") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Tianmubaseballstadium01.jpg/220px-Tianmubaseballstadium01.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tianmubaseballstadium01.jpg) [Tianmu Baseball Stadium](/wiki/Tianmu_Baseball_Stadium "Tianmu Baseball Stadium")

[Wei Chuan Dragons](/wiki/Wei_Chuan_Dragons "Wei Chuan Dragons") of Taiwan's [Chinese Professional Baseball League](/wiki/Chinese_Professional_Baseball_League "Chinese Professional Baseball League") is a professional baseball team based in Taipei.^[\[126\]](#cite_note-129)^ The Taipei Highwealth team of the [Popcorn League](/wiki/Popcorn_League "Popcorn League") is also based in Taipei, co-sponsored by the Taipei City Government and Highwealth Construction.{#cite_ref-129}

Taipei also has two professional basketball teams, the [Taipei Taishin Mars](/wiki/Taipei_Taishin_Mars "Taipei Taishin Mars") of the [T1 League](/wiki/T1_League "T1 League")^[\[127\]](#cite_note-130)^ and the [Taipei Fubon Braves](/wiki/Taipei_Fubon_Braves "Taipei Fubon Braves") of the [P. League+](/wiki/P._League%2B "P. League+").^[\[128\]](#cite_note-131)^{#cite_ref-131}  

### Major sporting events {#Major_sporting_events}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Major sporting events")\]

Below is a selected list of recent sporting events hosted by the city:

* [2004 FIFA Futsal World Championship](/wiki/2004_FIFA_Futsal_World_Championship "2004 FIFA Futsal World Championship")
* [2006 Women's Baseball World Cup](/wiki/2006_Women%27s_Baseball_World_Cup "2006 Women's Baseball World Cup")
* [2007 Baseball World Cup](/wiki/2007_Baseball_World_Cup "2007 Baseball World Cup")
* [2009 Asian Judo Championships](/wiki/2009_Asian_Judo_Championships "2009 Asian Judo Championships")
* [2009 Summer Deaflympics](/wiki/2009_Summer_Deaflympics "2009 Summer Deaflympics")
* [2013 Badminton Asia Championships](/wiki/2013_Badminton_Asia_Championships "2013 Badminton Asia Championships")
* [2015 WBSC Premier12](/wiki/2015_WBSC_Premier12 "2015 WBSC Premier12")
* [2016 IIHF Women's Challenge Cup of Asia Division I](/wiki/2016_IIHF_Women%27s_Challenge_Cup_of_Asia_Division_I "2016 IIHF Women's Challenge Cup of Asia Division I")
* [2017 Summer Universiade](/wiki/2017_Summer_Universiade "2017 Summer Universiade")
* [2019 Asian Men's Club Volleyball Championship](/wiki/2019_Asian_Men%27s_Club_Volleyball_Championship "2019 Asian Men's Club Volleyball Championship")
* [2022 U-23 Baseball World Cup](/wiki/2022_U-23_Baseball_World_Cup "2022 U-23 Baseball World Cup") (co-hosted with Taichung and [Yunlin](/wiki/Yunlin_County "Yunlin County"))
* [2023 Asian Men's Volleyball Challenge Cup](/wiki/2023_Asian_Men%27s_Volleyball_Challenge_Cup "2023 Asian Men's Volleyball Challenge Cup")
* [2023 IKF World Korfball Championship](/wiki/2023_IKF_World_Korfball_Championship "2023 IKF World Korfball Championship")
* [2023 U-18 Baseball World Cup](/wiki/2023_U-18_Baseball_World_Cup "2023 U-18 Baseball World Cup") (Co-hosted with Taichung)
* [2024 World Junior Figure Skating Championships](/wiki/2024_World_Junior_Figure_Skating_Championships "2024 World Junior Figure Skating Championships")
* [2025 Summer World Masters Games](/wiki/2025_Summer_World_Masters_Games "2025 Summer World Masters Games") (co-host with New Taipei City)
* [Taipei Marathon](/wiki/Taipei_Marathon "Taipei Marathon") (annual): The marathon is one of the two [World Athletics Label Road Races](/wiki/World_Athletics_Label_Road_Races "World Athletics Label Road Races") in Taiwan, being categorized as an Elite Label Road Race. The other race is the [New Taipei City Wan Jin Shi Marathon](/wiki/New_Taipei_City_Wan_Jin_Shi_Marathon "New Taipei City Wan Jin Shi Marathon"), categorized as a Gold Label Road Race.^[\[129\]](#cite_note-132)^{#cite_ref-132}

The [Taipei Arena](/wiki/Taipei_Arena "Taipei Arena") is located at the site of the former [Taipei Municipal Baseball Stadium](/wiki/Taipei_Municipal_Baseball_Stadium "Taipei Municipal Baseball Stadium") (demolished in 2000), with a capacity of over 15,000. It was opened on 1 December 2005 and has since held more art and cultural activities (such as live concerts) than sporting events, which it was originally designed for.^[\[130\]](#cite_note-133)^ The [Chinese Taipei Ice Hockey League](/wiki/Chinese_Taipei_Ice_Hockey_League "Chinese Taipei Ice Hockey League") plays out of the auxiliary arena.{#cite_ref-133}

[Taipei Dome](/wiki/Taipei_Dome "Taipei Dome") and [Tianmu Baseball Stadium](/wiki/Tianmu_Baseball_Stadium "Tianmu Baseball Stadium") are the major baseball venues in Taipei. The [Taipei Dome](/wiki/Taipei_Dome "Taipei Dome"), which has the capacity to house 40,071 seats, is estimated to finish construction by the end of 2023.^[\[131\]](#cite_note-134)^{#cite_ref-134}

[Taipei Municipal Stadium](/wiki/Taipei_Municipal_Stadium "Taipei Municipal Stadium") is a [multipurpose stadium](/wiki/Multipurpose_stadium "Multipurpose stadium") that hosts football and track and field events, as well as concerts, both live and prerecorded.^[\[132\]](#cite_note-MyUser_Https:_December_12_2020c-135)^ Originally built in 1956, it was demolished and reconstructed in 2009.^[\[133\]](#cite_note-136)^{#cite_ref-136}  

### Youth baseball {#Youth_baseball}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Youth baseball")\]

In 2010, a Taipei baseball team---Chung-Ching Junior Little League---won the [Junior League World Series](/wiki/Junior_League_World_Series#List_of_champions "Junior League World Series"). The achievement came after winning the Asia-Pacific Region, then defeating the Mexico Region and Latin America Region champions to become the International champion, and finally defeating the U.S. champion (Southwest Region), Rose Capital East LL (Tyler, Texas), 9--1.^[\[134\]](#cite_note-137)^ Taiwan's [Little League World Series](/wiki/Little_League_World_Series "Little League World Series") international team has won 17 championships, the most wins in the league.^[\[135\]](#cite_note-138)^{#cite_ref-138}  

Media {#Media}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Media")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG/220px-Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG)](/wiki/File:Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG) TVBS-G produces programs mainly from their [Nangang](/wiki/Nangang_District,_Taipei "Nangang District, Taipei") building in [Taipei City](/wiki/Taipei_City "Taipei City").

As the capital, Taipei City is the headquarters for many television and radio stations in Taiwan and the center of some of the country's largest newspapers.  

### Television {#Television}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Television")\]

Television stations located in Taipei include the [CTS Education and Culture](/wiki/CTS_Education_and_Culture "CTS Education and Culture"), [CTS Recreation](/wiki/CTS_Recreation "CTS Recreation"), [CTV MyLife](/wiki/CTV_MyLife "CTV MyLife"), [CTV News Channel](/wiki/CTV_News_Channel_(Taiwan) "CTV News Channel (Taiwan)"), [China Television](/wiki/China_Television "China Television"), [Chinese Television System](/wiki/Chinese_Television_System "Chinese Television System"), [Chung T'ien Television](/wiki/Chung_T%27ien_Television "Chung T'ien Television"), [Dimo TV](/wiki/Dimo_TV "Dimo TV"), [Eastern Television](/wiki/Eastern_Television "Eastern Television"), [Era Television](/wiki/Era_Television "Era Television"), [FTV News](/wiki/FTV_News "FTV News"), [Follow Me TV](/wiki/Follow_Me_TV_(Taiwan) "Follow Me TV (Taiwan)"), [Formosa TV](/wiki/Formosa_TV "Formosa TV"), [Gala Television](/wiki/Gala_Television "Gala Television"), [Public Television Service](/wiki/Public_Television_Service "Public Television Service"), [SET Metro](/wiki/SET_Metro "SET Metro"), [SET News](/wiki/SET_News "SET News"), [SET Taiwan](/wiki/SET_Taiwan "SET Taiwan"), [Sanlih E-Television](/wiki/Sanlih_E-Television "Sanlih E-Television"), [Shuang Xing](/wiki/Shuang_Xing "Shuang Xing"), [TTV Family](/wiki/TTV_Family "TTV Family"), [TTV Finance](/wiki/TTV_Finance "TTV Finance"), [TTV World](/wiki/TTV_World "TTV World"), [TVBS](/wiki/TVBS "TVBS"), [TVBS-G](/wiki/TVBS-G "TVBS-G"), [TVBS-NEWS](/wiki/TVBS-NEWS "TVBS-NEWS"), [Taiwan Broadcasting System](/wiki/Taiwan_Broadcasting_System "Taiwan Broadcasting System"), [Videoland Television Network](/wiki/Videoland_Television_Network "Videoland Television Network") and [Taiwan Television](/wiki/Taiwan_Television "Taiwan Television").  

### Newspapers {#Newspapers}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Newspapers")\]

Newspapers include *[Apple Daily](/wiki/Apple_Daily_(Taiwan) "Apple Daily (Taiwan)")* , *[Central Daily News](/wiki/Central_Daily_News "Central Daily News")* , *[The China Post](/wiki/The_China_Post "The China Post")* , *[China Times](/wiki/China_Times "China Times")* , *[DigiTimes](/wiki/DigiTimes "DigiTimes")* , *[Kinmen Daily News](/wiki/Kinmen_Daily_News "Kinmen Daily News")* , *[Liberty Times](/wiki/Liberty_Times "Liberty Times")* , *[Mandarin Daily News](/wiki/Mandarin_Daily_News "Mandarin Daily News")* , *[Matsu Daily](/wiki/Matsu_Daily "Matsu Daily")* , *[Min Sheng Bao](/wiki/Min_Sheng_Bao "Min Sheng Bao")* , *[Sharp Daily](/wiki/Sharp_Daily "Sharp Daily")* , *[Taipei Times](/wiki/Taipei_Times "Taipei Times")* , *[Taiwan Daily](/wiki/Taiwan_Daily "Taiwan Daily")* , *[Taiwan News](/wiki/Taiwan_News "Taiwan News")* , *[Taiwan Times](/wiki/Taiwan_Times "Taiwan Times")* and *[United Daily News](/wiki/United_Daily_News "United Daily News")*.  

International relations {#International_relations}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: International relations")\]

Taipei was a member of the [Asian Network of Major Cities 21](/wiki/Asian_Network_of_Major_Cities_21 "Asian Network of Major Cities 21") before its dissolvement.

### Friendship cities {#Friendship_cities}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Friendship cities")\]

* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png) [Perth](/wiki/Perth "Perth"), [Western Australia](/wiki/Western_Australia "Western Australia"), Australia (1999)^[\[137\]](#cite_note-TaipeiTwin-140)^{#cite_ref-TaipeiTwin_140-2}
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png) [Gyeonggi-do](/wiki/Gyeonggi_Province "Gyeonggi Province"), South Korea (2000)
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png) [Orange County](/wiki/Orange_County,_California "Orange County, California"), [CA](/wiki/California "California"), United States (2000)^[\[137\]](#cite_note-TaipeiTwin-140)^{#cite_ref-TaipeiTwin_140-3}
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png) [George Town](/wiki/George_Town,_Penang "George Town, Penang"), [Penang](/wiki/Penang "Penang"), Malaysia (2009)
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Finland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Finland.svg.png) [Helsinki](/wiki/Helsinki "Helsinki"), Finland (2012)^[\[137\]](#cite_note-TaipeiTwin-140)^{#cite_ref-TaipeiTwin_140-4}

In popular culture {#In_popular_culture}
----------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: In popular culture")\]

* Taipei's name is used in a [professional wrestling](/wiki/Professional_wrestling "Professional wrestling") match named the "Taipei Deathmatch" in which the wrestlers' fists are taped and dipped into glue and in broken and crushed glass, allowing shards to stick to their fists. This match can be won by pinfall, submission or escape.^[\[148\]](#cite_note-taip-151)^{#cite_ref-taip_151-0}
* Writer [Tao Lin](/wiki/Tao_Lin "Tao Lin")'s 2013 novel is titled [*Taipei*](/wiki/Taipei_(novel) "Taipei (novel)") and takes place in both New York City and Taipei, where the protagonist Paul's parents were born and live. In the novel, the character named Paul gets married and then visits Taipei with his new wife. They take MDMA and LSD and film a mock documentary on "Taiwan's first McDonald's."^[\[149\]](#cite_note-152)^ The novel was made into a movie titled *High Resolution* , starring [Justin Chon](/wiki/Justin_Chon "Justin Chon") and [Ellie Bamber](/wiki/Ellie_Bamber "Ellie Bamber").^[\[150\]](#cite_note-153)^{#cite_ref-153}

Notes {#Notes}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Notes")\]  

### Words in native languages {#Words_in_native_languages}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Words in native languages")\]  
1. \^ [^***a***^](#cite_ref-word1_1-0) [^***b***^](#cite_ref-word1_1-1)
   * [Traditional Chinese script](/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 臺北市
   * [Mandarin](/wiki/Taiwanese_Mandarin "Taiwanese Mandarin") [Pinyin](/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): *Táiběi Shì*
   * [Hokkien](/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien "Taiwanese Hokkien"): *Tâi-pak Tshī*
   * [Sixian](/wiki/Sixian_dialect "Sixian dialect") Hakka: *Tǒi-běd Sii*
   * [Hailu](/wiki/Hailu_dialect "Hailu dialect") Hakka: *Toi-bed Shi^+^*
   {#cite_note-word1-1}
{#cite_note-word1-1}  

### Other {#Other}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Taipei&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Other")\]  
1. **[\^](#cite_ref-9)** The [Constitution of the Republic of China](/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_China "Constitution of the Republic of China") does not stipulate any city, including Taipei or its pre-1949 capital, [Nanjing](/wiki/Nanjing "Nanjing"), as the *de jure* capital of the Republic of China. However, Taipei has been designated the official [seat of central government](/wiki/Seat_of_government "Seat of government") by a decree, thus making it the *de facto* capital.^[\[5\]](#cite_note-6)^^[\[6\]](#cite_note-7)^^[\[7\]](#cite_note-gov-8)^ Despite having no actual control, the [People's Republic of China](/wiki/China "China") considers Taipei to be the capital of its claimed [Taiwan Province](/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China "Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China").{#cite_ref-gov_8-0}
{#cite_note-9}
2. **[\^](#cite_ref-14)** The [Taiwan Provincial Government](/wiki/Taiwan_Provincial_Government "Taiwan Provincial Government") subsequently moved to [Zhongxing New Village](/wiki/Zhongxing_New_Village "Zhongxing New Village") in [Nantou County](/wiki/Nantou_County "Nantou County") until it was dissolved in 2018.{#cite_note-14}
{#cite_note-14}

| * ^1^ The provinces are merely retained as nominal entities within the constitutional structure, as they have no governing power following the formal dissolution of the provincial administrative organs in 2018. Cities and counties are de facto regarded as the principal constituent divisions of the ROC. * Sarah Shair-Rosenfield (November 2020). ["Taiwan Combined"](https://garymarks.web.unc.edu/wp-content/uploads/sites/13018/2021/03/Taiwan_combined.pdf) (PDF). The University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill.
